        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3296872529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13346498922282681122">The Prisoner of Heaven is the third volume in Ruiz Zafon's Cemetary of Forgotten Books series, at this stage, there is at least one more book. Like the previous two books, this book oozes atmosphere, the reader is taken on another scenic journey of Barcelona. But this one is a little different from the first two. In Shadow of the Wind and The Angel's Game we are introduced to the Sempere and Sons bookstore and the Cemetary of Forgotten Books. This volume returns us to the store and eventually th</span>
  <span id="freeText13346498922282681122" style="display:none">The Prisoner of Heaven is the third volume in Ruiz Zafon's Cemetary of Forgotten Books series, at this stage, there is at least one more book. Like the previous two books, this book oozes atmosphere, the reader is taken on another scenic journey of Barcelona. But this one is a little different from the first two. In Shadow of the Wind and The Angel's Game we are introduced to the Sempere and Sons bookstore and the Cemetary of Forgotten Books. This volume returns us to the store and eventually the Cemetary but it does not further the story, rather it retracts and enhances the history of the story.<br /><br />The bookstore has always had the helping hand of Fermin Romero de Torres as a loyal employee. His character has always been a major one within the four walls of the store but the overall plot of the series has followed the Sempere family. As Fermin approaches his wedding he begins to look at his life. The prisoner of Heaven, therefore, becomes mostly a historical novel of Fermin's life, following his early life up until he finds work in the bookstore and makes his lifelong friends. This completes the histories of all of the bookstore's staff.<br /><br />As I have yet to read the next book I can only guess that we need to know Fermin's history to further the story. If not, it is a very interesting history and an enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13346498922282681122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11090234239538388026" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book, though it was quite short. It basically just gives you backstory on characters from both <i>The Angel's Game</i> and <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>. <span id="freeTextContainer17275089162807984101"><b>Endangerment</b><br/>Prisoner of Heaven is the third enchanting story from Carlos Ruiz Zafon's, Cemetery of Forgotten Books trilogy and it continues with the same edgy atmosphere as the previous 2 books. There is always a sense of darkness and secrets with these stories and Zafon is a master of keeping the flow of suspicion and intrigue alive throughout a book.<br/><br/>Characters from the other books return, but this book is mainly focused on Ferm√≠n who works with Daniel in the bookshop. The story begins when an </span>
  <span id="freeText17275089162807984101" style="display:none"><b>Endangerment</b><br />Prisoner of Heaven is the third enchanting story from Carlos Ruiz Zafon's, Cemetery of Forgotten Books trilogy and it continues with the same edgy atmosphere as the previous 2 books. There is always a sense of darkness and secrets with these stories and Zafon is a master of keeping the flow of suspicion and intrigue alive throughout a book.<br /><br />Characters from the other books return, but this book is mainly focused on Ferm√≠n who works with Daniel in the bookshop. The story begins when an unsavoury character purchasing a special edition of the Count of Monte Cristo from Daniel, insists on buying the most expensive book in the store. Was his choice a prophetic warning of what lay ahead, especially when he added the inscription?<br /><i> For Ferm√≠n Romero de Torres, who came back from among the dead and holds the key to the future. </i><br /><br />Ferm√≠n is a secretive person and as it transpires he spent time in a prison cell along with David Martin, of Angles Game. He shares his past insights and events with Daniel as they seek to solve this puzzle. The twists and turns will need to be discovered by the next reader but to immerse yourself in Zafron‚Äôs melodic writing is a memorable experience. His books have a habit of living with you and giving you that chill in your back. It‚Äôs not horror it‚Äôs just a stalking menace that threatens to invade when you‚Äôre not vigilant.</span>

<div id="review_357601262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357601262" />
    <a title="Kelly Hager" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1436215-kelly-hager"><img alt="Kelly Hager" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422502668p2/1436215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/357601262?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Hager" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Hager" href="/user/show/1436215-kelly-hager">Kelly Hager</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780297868101" href="/book/show/15725141-the-prisoner-of-heaven">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer357601262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1066345400840968239">The Shadow of the Wind is my favorite novel ever, and so when I learned there would be a companion novel, I could have cried. And then when I found out that Daniel and Bea would appear in another book? I think my Grinchy heart grew five sizes. Granted, this novel is more about Fermin but that's okay---I love Fermin!<br/><br/>The thing that I love most about Carlos Ruiz Zafon and this series is that he's written a love letter to books and to the people that read them. Pretty much everything that's good abo</span>
  <span id="freeText1066345400840968239" style="display:none">The Shadow of the Wind is my favorite novel ever, and so when I learned there would be a companion novel, I could have cried. And then when I found out that Daniel and Bea would appear in another book? I think my Grinchy heart grew five sizes. Granted, this novel is more about Fermin but that's okay---I love Fermin!<br /><br />The thing that I love most about Carlos Ruiz Zafon and this series is that he's written a love letter to books and to the people that read them. Pretty much everything that's good about humanity (and yes, what's bad about it, too) can be found in these pages. I know that's a bold statement, but it's true. <br /><br />They're about love and loyalty, hatred and despair, frienship and courage...but most of all, they're about books and how they can save us. <br /><br />I just finished The Prisoner of Heaven, but I am already looking forward to re-reading it. And I would love someday to accidentally stumble into the Cemetery of Forgotten Books. <br /><br />Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1066345400840968239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_409505894" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/409505894" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/409505894?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780297868101" href="/book/show/15725141-the-prisoner-of-heaven">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer409505894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7673902118064985029">It was very easy to give the maximum rating for the previuos books of the author using the Barcelona setting. I loved the characters, the use of language, the romantic entaglements of the heroes and the gothic mood. Much of these aspects are present in <b> The Prisoner of Heaven </b> and at the start I believed the book will be another addition to my favorites shelf. Now that I've finished it I believe the missing ingredient is plot, a coherent story, a point of focus to the narrative. As other reviewe</span>
  <span id="freeText7673902118064985029" style="display:none">It was very easy to give the maximum rating for the previuos books of the author using the Barcelona setting. I loved the characters, the use of language, the romantic entaglements of the heroes and the gothic mood. Much of these aspects are present in <b> The Prisoner of Heaven </b> and at the start I believed the book will be another addition to my favorites shelf. Now that I've finished it I believe the missing ingredient is plot, a coherent story, a point of focus to the narrative. As other reviewers already noticed, this feels like a filler, a rushed project to tie up some loose threads between the two major novels already published and to flesh out some secondary characters - nominally Fermin Romero de Torres, the protagonist here while Daniel Martin takes a more passive role of witness / observer. Best chapters in my opinion here are the ones dealing with the prison on Montjuic and the abuses of the Franco regime. I had hoped to have The Cemetery of Forgotten Books play a more important role, and count the sole chapter featuring it as another disappointment with the story.<br /><br />It is possible that some of my issues are derived from a hazy memory about the numerous events and characters from the previous novels referenced here. <b> The Prisoner of Heaven </b> doesn't really work as a standalone book, as it tries to establish stronger links between <b> The Shadow of the Wind </b> and <b> The Angel's Game </b>, as well as prepare the ground for the next installment. In fact, I'm pretty sure I will rate it higher when the series is completed and I will be able to re-read the books one after the other.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7673902118064985029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Doug Bradshaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/808994-doug-bradshaw"><img alt="Doug Bradshaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548429066p2/808994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356025010?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug Bradshaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug Bradshaw" href="/user/show/808994-doug-bradshaw">Doug Bradshaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356025010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5070695572832764401">If you loved Shadow of the Wind like I did, you'll love this book. It is the perfect follow up book with Fermin and Daniel starring and Martin is also there in the background as well as Isabella. The story goes through Femin's imprisonment and difficult life and his role in Daniel's life. It is touching, funny, and profound in its own way. I love this author and can't wait for the next book. Here are some random comments:<br/><br/>1. Half of the enjoyment of this book is Fermin's clever lines and observat</span>
  <span id="freeText5070695572832764401" style="display:none">If you loved Shadow of the Wind like I did, you'll love this book. It is the perfect follow up book with Fermin and Daniel starring and Martin is also there in the background as well as Isabella. The story goes through Femin's imprisonment and difficult life and his role in Daniel's life. It is touching, funny, and profound in its own way. I love this author and can't wait for the next book. Here are some random comments:<br /><br />1. Half of the enjoyment of this book is Fermin's clever lines and observations about people and life. They are spot on and poetically written. He is a real wordsmith.<br /><br />2. You can tell sometimes that it is translated but there is something enjoyable about the way it has been done. It seems like some translations may take a little bit away from what the author is trying to say where here, I think we get the whole story. <br /><br />3. It is still a coming of age story except that Daniel is in his twenties now and has been married for a while. Nevertheless, Fermin is there to help him find his way through the adult world. He is protected and helped by this crazy guy and it is touching.<br /><br />4. Makes you want to get back to Barcelona to spend more time there in the restaurants and bars and stay up all night with friends.<br /><br />5. The great vault of the lost books appears again. Love that place. I could write a spoiler here but I won't.<br /><br />This is a book you can read in a few days. Read it after you've read Shadow of the Wind and Angel's Game. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5070695572832764401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer443587216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13752177915493198892">I liked this third volume of the series better than ‚ÄúThe Shadow of the Wind‚Äù and ‚ÄúThe Angel‚Äôs Game‚Äù due to its simpler, less labyrinthine plot. I was captivated by this wonderful story of the power of friendship, love, and sacrifice engagingly written with warmth and humor. It also shines with old fashioned adventures and a prose style hearkening back to tales written by Dumas.<br/><br/>Daniel Sempere, who runs a bookstore in Barcelona with his father in the late 50‚Äôs, receives a threatening visit and mys</span>
  <span id="freeText13752177915493198892" style="display:none">I liked this third volume of the series better than ‚ÄúThe Shadow of the Wind‚Äù and ‚ÄúThe Angel‚Äôs Game‚Äù due to its simpler, less labyrinthine plot. I was captivated by this wonderful story of the power of friendship, love, and sacrifice engagingly written with warmth and humor. It also shines with old fashioned adventures and a prose style hearkening back to tales written by Dumas.<br /><br />Daniel Sempere, who runs a bookstore in Barcelona with his father in the late 50‚Äôs, receives a threatening visit and mysterious message for his employee and dear friend Fermin. His detective work leads him to dig out a story from Fermin of survival and commitment involving a writer friend of Daniel‚Äôs deceased mother, David Martin. Fermin‚Äôs story harks back to the period of Fascist oppression from 1939 to 1941, which includes a long period of imprisonment.<br /> <br />Though this structure, this novel links extensively with the previous two novels and helps elucidate the paths taken by their characters. I look forward to the fourth and final novel in the series.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4729415716480425555">Zafon is a master storyteller with gorgeous prose. Brilliant. My only complaint with Prisoner is I wish it had been longer because I wasn‚Äôt ready for the book to end. This is Fermin‚Äôs story, one of my favorite characters in the series. It‚Äôs more straightforward without the twists and turns in Shadow of the Wind and Angel‚Äôs Game, and it certainly whets my appetite for #4.   <span id="freeText4729415716480425555" style="display:none">Zafon is a master storyteller with gorgeous prose. Brilliant. My only complaint with Prisoner is I wish it had been longer because I wasn‚Äôt ready for the book to end. This is Fermin‚Äôs story, one of my favorite characters in the series. It‚Äôs more straightforward without the twists and turns in Shadow of the Wind and Angel‚Äôs Game, and it certainly whets my appetite for #4. This series is one of the few that I would consider re-reading at some point. They are books to curl up with and lose yourself in the story.<br /><br />P.S. In considering Shadow of the Wind now that it's a few years out and I've just finished the 3rd book in the series I'm going back and changing my rating to 5 stars.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Kgk9uBT7M52btOovsP5IghCn0nWIq2qF3wXHdabxdfGo3HuZS9GEQTQuAHvqd+kEGXfTOTWWsgmayk3wTiWVAw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MM3iE8j7glWXkXxrQuLVfEtmSVBF3Jyx2lxybOWqNUayGKQyl9E1iTgLlj8Ya3T6QrZIHPjhRD2fk/jpDX7VtA==')})
  }

          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class='navButtonArrow sliderArrowPrev'></div>
</div>
